<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17096138369914086020">Stanley Yelnats is under a curse. A curse that began with his no-good-dirty-rotten-pig-stealing-great-great-grandfather and has since followed generations of Yelnatses. Now Stanley has been unjustly sent to a boys’ detention center, Camp Green Lake, where the boys build character by spending all day, every day digging holes exactly five feet wide and five feet deep. There</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17096138369914086020">Stanley Yelnats is under a curse. A curse that began with his no-good-dirty-rotten-pig-stealing-great-great-grandfather and has since followed generations of Yelnatses. Now Stanley has been unjustly sent to a boys’ detention center, Camp Green Lake, where the boys build character by spending all day, every day digging holes exactly five feet wide and five feet deep. There is no lake at Camp Green Lake. But there are an awful lot of holes.<br /><br />It doesn’t take long for Stanley to realize there’s more than character improvement going on at Camp Green Lake. The boys are digging holes because the warden is looking for something. But what could be buried under a dried-up lake? Stanley tries to dig up the truth in this inventive and darkly humorous tale of crime and punishment—and redemption.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17096138369914086020">...more</a>

            if ($('edition_444312').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});

      $('edition_444312').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_262500481">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262500481" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie" class="left imgcol" title="Catie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" alt="Catie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/262500481?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie" class="user" title="Catie">Catie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=children-s" class="actionLinkLite">children-s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=middle-grade" class="actionLinkLite">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2012" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer262500481">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15383221668821923436">I am very sad that I never read this as a young person, because I think that I would have loved it even more than I do now. I think that it probably would have blown my mind. I have to applaud Louis Sachar for being so courageous in a children’s novel.<br /><br />Effortlessly weaving together the past, present, and ancient history of these characters, Mr. Sachar examines the impact of our history and the nature of hope and human compassion, all while maintaining a light, humorous quality. This is a book for</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15383221668821923436">I am very sad that I never read this as a young person, because I think that I would have loved it even more than I do now. I think that it probably would have blown my mind. I have to applaud Louis Sachar for being so courageous in a children’s novel.<br /><br />Effortlessly weaving together the past, present, and ancient history of these characters, Mr. Sachar examines the impact of our history and the nature of hope and human compassion, all while maintaining a light, humorous quality. This is a book for children, but one that never speaks down to children. It is both mature and youthful.<br /><br />Stanley is tried and convicted for a crime that he didn’t commit, sent to a reform camp for boys, and forced to work day after day in the hot sun digging holes – without any hope of aid. He’s treated callously and unfairly, but he must learn to keep going, get along with the boys around him, and survive. <br /><br />This is not a book that promises (like so many other children’s books do) success and rewards for good behavior, for choosing all the right paths. That’s not what real living, real maturity is all about. It’s about learning to deal with adversity and tragedy and failure when they come – because they will. It’s about making the right choices even when there are no rewards, no promised successes, simply because they’re right. And more than that – it’s about choosing kindness and compassion, even when everything around you is hard and unfair. <br /><br />The only part of this novel that I don’t quite like is the ending, which seems to undermine the more realistic quality of the rest of the novel. I wish that Stanley and Hector could survive happily without a fairy tale ending, because after all of that, they know that they don’t need one to be happy. But I think that as a child, I would have enjoyed seeing them win the day.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Brett Dennen – <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=T1CyvfTVhc8">Darlin’ Do Not Fear</a><br /><br />This is a very sweet song about growing up and holding onto hope during the hard times.<br /><br /><em>Your confidence is faultless your faith etched in stone <br />and neither could comfort you from the wild unknown <br />So bury your burning hatred like a hatchet in the snow <br />Darlin' do not fear what you don't really know</em><br /><br />Also seen on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/holes-by-louis-sachar.html">The Readventurer</a>.<br /><br />Stop by for <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/02/book-vs-movie-holes-by-louis-sachar.html">a comparison</a> of this book to the movie version!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15383221668821923436">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_239187835">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239187835" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5686305-shayantani-das" class="left imgcol" title="Shayantani Das"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1436246159p2/5686305.jpg" alt="Shayantani Das" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/239187835?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 26, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5686305-shayantani-das" class="user" title="Shayantani Das">Shayantani Das</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5686305-shayantani-das?shelf=suspense-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">suspense-mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5686305-shayantani-das?shelf=favorite-protagonist" class="actionLinkLite">favorite-protagonist</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5686305-shayantani-das?shelf=well-developed-plot" class="actionLinkLite">well-developed-plot</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5686305-shayantani-das?shelf=the-eternal-quest" class="actionLinkLite">the-eternal-quest</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5686305-shayantani-das?shelf=excellent-prose" class="actionLinkLite">excellent-prose</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer239187835">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10819203635237854364">No wonder this book has got a Newberry Award. Its 200 something pages of pure awesomeness! By beautifully executing such an ingenious concept, Louis Sachar has made me his fan.<br /><br />Stanley Yelnats is an over sized preteen who is falsely accused of stealing. He is provided with the option to choose between jail and camp green lake. Stanley is not well of, and has never been to camp, so his choice is obvious. Unfortunately though, Camp green lake is not the usual camp. He gets his fair share of adventu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10819203635237854364">No wonder this book has got a Newberry Award. Its 200 something pages of pure awesomeness! By beautifully executing such an ingenious concept, Louis Sachar has made me his fan.<br /><br />Stanley Yelnats is an over sized preteen who is falsely accused of stealing. He is provided with the option to choose between jail and camp green lake. Stanley is not well of, and has never been to camp, so his choice is obvious. Unfortunately though, Camp green lake is not the usual camp. He gets his fair share of adventure from the camp, <strong>only it comes in totally unexpected ways.</strong><br /><br />What I liked best was the flow of the novel. Stanley is a narrator one can sympathize with. Him being not whinny comes as a welcome relief. Even in the face of grave danger, he remains his calm self with his dry sense of humor, blaming his "no-good-dirty-rotten-pig-stealing-great-great-grandfather" for almost everything. Zero and his friendship were also refreshing to read about. (The mutually beneficial and constructive kind)<br /><br />Then there are parts in the novel when, the story behind the Lake’s history, and its residents were elaborated. I think, they were my favorite parts as they reminded me of my grandmother and the times when she used to tell me stories. The tone of the story automatically gets you in this really relaxed mode and when you are done reading, you have this really satisfied smile on your face. <br /><img width="400" height="400" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363721i/715194._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><strong> Not exactly how I imagined it, but yeah! Something like that! </strong><br /><br />A warning though: When you read the book, don’t bring along your microscopes and start pondering about why there are too many coincidences towards the end. Just enjoy this really awesome book, chill and get yourself a good mood.<br /><br />.<strong>4.5 stars</strong><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10819203635237854364">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_29738559">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29738559" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1376766-becky" class="left imgcol" title="Becky"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446571694p2/1376766.jpg" alt="Becky" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/29738559?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1376766-becky" class="user" title="Becky">Becky</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2224888.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439253222" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer29738559">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5192673409204056917">Funny story: I'm trying to shelve this book, and can't remember if it had been banned (but I thought it had - google confirmed). At the same time, my friend Allison and I are chatting on Google Chat, and she starts ranting about how ridiculous book banning is (an opinion with which I agree wholeheartedly). Anyway, the conversation went like this: <br /><br /><em>me: Is Holes a banned book? I can't remember<br />allison: dunno... the whole concept of banned books is stupid. I mean, you could find a reason to gripe abo</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5192673409204056917">Funny story: I'm trying to shelve this book, and can't remember if it had been banned (but I thought it had - google confirmed). At the same time, my friend Allison and I are chatting on Google Chat, and she starts ranting about how ridiculous book banning is (an opinion with which I agree wholeheartedly). Anyway, the conversation went like this: <br /><br /><em>me: Is Holes a banned book? I can't remember<br />allison: dunno... the whole concept of banned books is stupid. I mean, you could find a reason to gripe about any book<br />me: yes, I agree<br />allison: I think The Replacement should be banned because there is a scene talking about knives in the kitchen<br />allison: VIOLENCE<br />me: haha just wait<br />allison: and he sits on his roof<br />allison: DANGEROUS BEHAVIOR<br />allison: RECKLESS<br />me: He says the F word, and there are BOOBIES!<br />allison: PORNOGRAPHY<br />me: IMMORALITY!<br />allison: lol<br />allison: or you could go the other way and be totally ridiculous<br />allison: Holes doesn't directly support a gay lifestyle<br />allison: BAN IT<br />me: But it does...<br />allison: oh well then uh...<br />me: all those boys are in and out of holes all day long</em><br /><br />Needless to say, there was laughter. Sometimes I crack myself up. <br /><br />Anyway, all witty repartee aside, I really liked this book. I have no idea why it would have been banned unless it was because a kid hits a jerk in the face with a shovel for being a complete ass to him day in and day out? That's probably it. ENCOURAGING VIOLENT BEHAVIOR AND DISRESPECT FOR AUTHORITY! BAN IT!<br /><br />I loved Stanley, but in all truth, I loved Zero more. He was the star of this show for me. I wanted everything to work out for him, and I was on pins and needles worrying about him when things started to go bad for him. I mean, these kids committed crimes, or at least they were accused of committing crimes, but they weren't BAD or EVIL. Punishment is one thing, but the kind of things that these kids were made to do is nothing short of abuse. And what's sad is that probably isn't a far stretch from what really happens - although probably for different reasons. <br /><br />I enjoyed how the three different storylines all came together in this one, and seeing the little bits of each one felt like discovering a gem. I'd have this, "OH!" moment each time something was revealed that linked something else... Really fun to read. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this one, and I look forward to seeing the movie soon, since I hear from Allison that it's fabulous. :)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5192673409204056917">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_154903483">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154903483" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/299871-ranee" class="left imgcol" title="Ranee"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1408710650p2/299871.jpg" alt="Ranee" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/154903483?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 30, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/299871-ranee" class="user" title="Ranee">Ranee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154903483">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1140979734376133860">I knew of a friend who lost everything when her father started digging holes. You see, her dad was a treasure hunter. And to be a treasure hunter, you are supposed to be well equipped and with good manpower. You must also be in possession of a reliable map and a lot of time. You also need a lot of money to be able to acquire all the above things. Unfortunately, my friend's father only acquired a fake map, swindlers for company and equipment worth nothing when you're digging the wrong hole. Littl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1140979734376133860">I knew of a friend who lost everything when her father started digging holes. You see, her dad was a treasure hunter. And to be a treasure hunter, you are supposed to be well equipped and with good manpower. You must also be in possession of a reliable map and a lot of time. You also need a lot of money to be able to acquire all the above things. Unfortunately, my friend's father only acquired a fake map, swindlers for company and equipment worth nothing when you're digging the wrong hole. Little by little, my friend's dad used up all their savings and even lost his time for their family. My friend and her siblings grew up and away from their dad. All was lost, true. All that was left is a hole in my friend's heart. There was once a treasure there, I am sure but her father dug too deep it failed to see it sparkle.<br /><br />The Hole I've read however is not my friend's story. It did not have a treasure map but it has a great plot. It did talk of treasures, the more obvious would be the one buried. There's a treasure in the form of friendship, one covered in perseverance and another enclosed with hope. If you add a bit of dust of fate with these treasures, you will get the story of a boy named Stanley Yelnats, the main protagonist in this novel. <br /><br />I liked the presentation of the story- the interconnectedness of their experiences. It's an application of Newton's 3rd law of motion (which states that for every action there is an equal and opposite reaction). Just like how someone else's athlete's foot become the reason for another's sweet riches; how the despair of having been bullied be the same reason for his freedom; or how being the teacher, he actually got the better lesson, more than he has bargained for. Stanley did that and in the end he gained friends and respect. All in all, Holes is not about big excavations, it's about filling the gaps. It talked about racism, crossing beyond borders. It talked about family and camaraderie. It talked about keeping your promises and breaking barriers. It talked about being a better person. And yes, even added the perks of enjoying a big onion bulb. <br /><br />When someone digs a hole out there in the vast universe, there'd be a lot of soil/dirt displaced. Imagine them as stories unburdened from some remote keeper. So what do we do with these soil/dirt/story? We place them inside our own gaps, enriching us such that our hole becomes full, we come out as a whole person.<br /><br />PS.<br />IF you wonder about my friend, last time I've heard, their parents are together again. He quit hunting for treasures and stuck with those that are far more precious, his own family.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1140979734376133860">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/444312.Holes" title="Hardcover 9780374332655" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/810660-kristenr?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/810660-kristenr?shelf=read-with-maya" class="actionLinkLite">read-with-maya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/810660-kristenr?shelf=male-author" class="actionLinkLite">male-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer123719442">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9540013885965900039">I'm not sure exactly when it happened, but it seems I'm no longer absolutely cool in my daughter's eyes. I could understand if her particular issues with me were current fashion or "the" things to do while hanging out with friends, but books? BOOKS?!? Oh, the pain!<br /><br />I don't say anything about the girly girl preteen drivel she loves to read (after all, I occasionally read girly girl grownup drivel) and I recommend a wide range of books (while keeping in mind she doesn't have the same penchant for s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9540013885965900039">I'm not sure exactly when it happened, but it seems I'm no longer absolutely cool in my daughter's eyes. I could understand if her particular issues with me were current fashion or "the" things to do while hanging out with friends, but books? BOOKS?!? Oh, the pain!<br /><br />I don't say anything about the girly girl preteen drivel she loves to read (after all, I occasionally read girly girl grownup drivel) and I recommend a wide range of books (while keeping in mind she doesn't have the same penchant for sf/fantasy as I do.) She is a voracious reader, will happily read things her teacher recommends, and liked the books that 'Santa' gave her.<br /><br />So why does she sneer every time I hand her a book? (well, she doesn't sneer *every* time, sometimes it's just a withering look or a "nah, I don't think so") <br /><br />I'm not sure how I acquired this book, and it was one I hadn't read as a kid. I suggested that Maya and I read it together since we've been enjoying reading aloud at bedtime. <br /><br />She read the blurb on the cover, handed it back to me and said "Nah." <br /><br /> I said, "Let's give it a shot."<br /><br />"Oh, it's an award winner, isn't it...uh uh," she replied.<br /><br />I then said, "Uh huh, we're giving this a shot."<br /><br />Cue withering look.<br /><br />The book quickly won her over. The short chapters are perfect for bedtime reading...we never had to stop in the middle of a chapter, and most nights read several chapters. <br /><br />The author weaves together several plots. Each thread is connected, but he deftly gives us just the bits of information we need at any given point, and it all comes together at the end wonderfully. I loved when Maya would make a connection and exclaim, "Oh - those are Sam's onions!" or gasp, "Oh no! That's what really happened?!"<br /><br />Final verdict? She loved it, and so did I.<br /><br />Apparently I am capable of choosing good books.<br /><br />Not that she'll remember that when I hand her the next book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9540013885965900039">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_22779539">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22779539" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/733629-chris" class="left imgcol" title="Chris"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1199331851p2/733629.jpg" alt="Chris" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/22779539?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 01, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/733629-chris" class="user" title="Chris">Chris</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer22779539">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13176355339375603696">I was picking up some books at the resale shop and for some reason found myself browsing in the children’s books. It seemed like the usual fare at first, some Dr. Seuss, a mangy copy of a Clifford book, a few ratty Choose Your Own Adventure paperbacks, Hugh Hefner’s autobiography, some smut called “The Very Virile Viking”, and “Pimp” by Iceberg Slim. Tucked amongst all this tawdry trash was something called “Holes”, which seemed to make sense sandwiched between “Pimp” and Hef’s life saga.<br /><br /> I soon</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13176355339375603696">I was picking up some books at the resale shop and for some reason found myself browsing in the children’s books. It seemed like the usual fare at first, some Dr. Seuss, a mangy copy of a Clifford book, a few ratty Choose Your Own Adventure paperbacks, Hugh Hefner’s autobiography, some smut called “The Very Virile Viking”, and “Pimp” by Iceberg Slim. Tucked amongst all this tawdry trash was something called “Holes”, which seemed to make sense sandwiched between “Pimp” and Hef’s life saga.<br /><br />	I soon realized that there was a movie based on this book made a few years back, which I had never bothered with, but, to my shock and awe, “Holes” was the work of Louis “Sideways-Stories” Sachar. As a long-time fan of the preposterous “Wayside School” stories, I immediately picked this up (along with the other aforementioned books) and decided to bump it up on my to-read list. I had no idea Sachar had even done any other work, and I was interested to see what he’d bring to the table.<br /><br />	I have to admit, I wasn’t nearly as impressed with “Holes” as I thought I might be. This might be due to the unrealistically high expectations I had based on my previous Sachar experience, or the fact that since they took the time and bankroll to make a movie based off this work, it obviously had to be incredible. <br /><br />	The palindromically-named Stanley Yelnats is a good-spirited and festively plump little kid who is shipped off to a boy’s reform program at Camp Green Lake as punishment for stealing a pair of shoes being donated to charity by Clyde “Sweet Feet” Livingston. However, poor Stanley never stole the shoes, he’s been wrongfully accused, which is something he’s accustomed to, since his family is under the influence of a malevolent gypsy curse which began due to an oversight by his no-good-dirty-rotten-pig-stealing-great-great-grandfather. This evil hex has brought misery and financial ruin to the Yelnats clan since it was first laid, and each male heir to the Yelnats throne vainly hopes to be the one to break this vicious cycle. It isn’t looking too promising for Stanley to be the chosen one, as he’s shipped off to Camp Green Lake, which is the dusty basin of a once-flourishing lake which has since dried up under the scorching desert sun. His duty at the Camp is torturous; each day he must wake up at cock-crow and dig a hole five feet deep by five feet wide, while eluding the venomous yellow-spotted lizards which infest the area. Spitting in each completed hole is optional, and Stanley opts for this luxury at the insistence of his peers.<br /><br />	The narrative of Stanley’s troubles at the camp are intertwined with the background of how this dread gypsy curse came about and also with the story of “Kissing” Katie Barlow, an outlaw that robbed his great-grandfather. While Stanley toils to dig hole after hole under the strict rule of the Warden and her lackeys (Mr. Pendanski and Mr. Sir), the tale of the curse unfolds, in which his great-great-grandfather Elya is vying for the hand of wealthy hottie Myra back in their motherland of Latvia. In order to win her hand, Myra’s father stipulates that the stud who presents the choicest pig as a gift will get the girl (which I hear is still a popular practice back in Riga), which leads Elya into cahoots with the gypsy, Madame Zeroni. Things take a turn for the worse for Elya, and he ends up not only forgetting to perform a favor for the gypsy, but he also gives away the hog as a wedding present to his rival. Even more spectacular is the downfall of the kind-hearted Katie Barlow, a benevolent teacher who begins an interracial relationship with an onionmonger named Sam in the Green Lake area. The ignorant townsfolk don’t cotton to this pairing and end up killing Sam (and his onion-chomping mule, Mary Lou), which leads the once-peaceful teacher to life as an outlaw. Barlow also happened to rob Stanley’s great-grandfather, and before kicking the bucket, she ended up burying all her ill-gotten gains somewhere in the parched and dry bowl of the former lake, a treasure yet to be unearthed that the Warden presumably is trying to locate with all this absurd hole-digging.<br /><br />	The story is pretty enjoyable, for the most part it follows in the silly tradition of the Sachar work I am familiar with, however, the fact that he had to throw a ‘message’ in there pretty much turned me off. Stanley and his fellow detainees at the Camp are a motley bunch, a mixed-race group of transgressors who are coming to terms with their own cultural identities. When Stanley makes an arrangement with black camper Zero to teach him to read in exchange for his labor, the others drop some ‘slave’ references. The saga of Katie Barlow and Sam, however, far eclipses this childish prattle, and firmly beats the reader of the head with the ‘love-your-brother’-stick. At one point, Sachar even states that god himself punished the intolerant populous of Green Lake using the 100 year drought that turned a thriving lake into a dust bowl. The whole race relations bit was generally annoying, and perhaps what might have bothered me most was that in his preaching, Sachar makes it clear how wrong it is to consider someone of color illiterate, stupid, or treacherous, but it’s fully acceptable to include the stereotype of a curse-casting gypsy thrown into the storyline. <br /><br />	Overall, the story comes together predictably and nicely, but the insistence with which Sachar clubbed me over the head with his ‘message’ bothered me.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13176355339375603696">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/688398-mary-taitt" class="left imgcol" title="Mary Taitt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1209478578p2/688398.jpg" alt="Mary Taitt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14611268?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/688398-mary-taitt" class="user" title="Mary Taitt">Mary Taitt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mary by: </span>
      Erwin
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/688398-mary-taitt?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14611268">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16483666529407725655">Holes, by Louis Sachar, 5/5. It was really good; I loved it. It's a young adult novel from which a movie was made. I have not seen the movie, but I hope to. The book is a Newberry Award Winner.<br /><br />Stanley Yelnats is falsely accused of stealing a pair of sneakers and set to Camp Green Lake, for criminal boys. To build character, the boys get up at 4:30 every morning and dig holes--big holes. If they find anything unusual, they are supposed to report it. But the warden isn't looking for fossils or pre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16483666529407725655">Holes, by Louis Sachar, 5/5. It was really good; I loved it. It's a young adult novel from which a movie was made. I have not seen the movie, but I hope to. The book is a Newberry Award Winner.<br /><br />Stanley Yelnats is falsely accused of stealing a pair of sneakers and set to Camp Green Lake, for criminal boys. To build character, the boys get up at 4:30 every morning and dig holes--big holes. If they find anything unusual, they are supposed to report it. But the warden isn't looking for fossils or pretty rocks. Something is going on other than character building, and Stanley wonders what they are looking for. The story is at once whimsical and dark, horrifying and funny, heartrending and heart-warming. There are rattlesnakes (one boy was been bitten and rushed to the hospital. He never comes back.) and many highly poisonous eleven-spotted yellow lizards with red eyes, black teeth and white tongues. We also learn about Stanley's no-good-dirty-rotten-pig-stealing great grandfather and the curse put on his family by the gypsy woman who was missing one pig, his grandfather who found refuge on God's thumb after being robbed by Kissing Kate Barlow, Kissing Kate herself and her handyman, Sam the onion man and how history does and doesn't affect the lives of living people. This many generational multiple story-lines slowly merge in unpredictable but delightful ways. We, the readers, meet a famous basketball player and an inventor and, of course, learn that bad boys are human, just like the rest of us, and sometimes even better than those not so confined. And we encounter inspiring courage fortitude and strength. 2/4/08</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16483666529407725655">...more</a>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/886144-brigid-flying-kick-a-pow?shelf=5-star-books" class="actionLinkLite">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/886144-brigid-flying-kick-a-pow?shelf=books-for-school" class="actionLinkLite">books-for-school</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/886144-brigid-flying-kick-a-pow?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/886144-brigid-flying-kick-a-pow?shelf=addicting-as-crack" class="actionLinkLite">addicting-as-crack</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/886144-brigid-flying-kick-a-pow?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/886144-brigid-flying-kick-a-pow?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/886144-brigid-flying-kick-a-pow?shelf=middle-grade" class="actionLinkLite">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15349910">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8929926173696880564">Holes is one of my favorite books of all time. The whole thing is just so clever. The writing style is simple, but not boring. Every character is amazingly developed and believable. I like how the story of the present and the story of the past connect to each other perfectly in the end. And the movie version is really good, too! I highly suggest this book to everyone. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_984403336">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984403336" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15462098-kaya" class="left imgcol" title="Kaya"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442356569p2/15462098.jpg" alt="Kaya" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/984403336?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15462098-kaya" class="user" title="Kaya">Kaya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/285943.Holes" title="Paperback 9780747544593" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer984403336">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15566014731318226314">Thoughtful and studious read. I can't say anything bad about the book, since every chapter made perfect sense. It just didn't bring out any emotion in me. Also, I found myself a bit bored throughout the flashbacks. Mostly, I think the biggest problem is that I'm too old for this book, even though I know it sounds a little pretentious. <br /><br />Stanley's family was cursed by a gypsy because of his great great great Pig-stealing-Grandpa. His dad tries to make a formula to get rid of the smell of old worn o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15566014731318226314">Thoughtful and studious read. I can't say anything bad about the book, since every chapter made perfect sense. It just didn't bring out any emotion in me. Also, I found myself a bit bored throughout the flashbacks. Mostly, I think the biggest problem is that I'm too old for this book, even though I know it sounds a little pretentious. <br /><br />Stanley's family was cursed by a gypsy because of his great great great Pig-stealing-Grandpa. His dad tries to make a formula to get rid of the smell of old worn out sneakers. Unfortunately, he's unsuccessful. Their family is poor and they can't afford to hire a good attorney for Stanley.<br /><br />Stanley is sent to Camp Green Lake as a punishment for a crime he didn't commit. He meets Zero there and a platonic bond is formed between the boys. Zero runs away from the camp and Stanley goes after him. Before that we've shown what a cruel place it really is when Stanley annoyed a guard. All the boys aligned in the hot sun to get their canteens filled with water and the guard hands Stanley's canteen back empty. Stanley even says "thank you" for it. <br /><br />The boys at the Camp are coming to terms with accepting their own identities and there is always underdeveloped tension between them. When Stanley makes an arrangement with Zero to teach him how to read in exchange for Zero's help in digging his hole, the others aren't particularly happy about it. What makes the story realistic is that nothing magical was going to help any of them escape, no adult was going to get Stanley and explain everything was a big mistake.<br /><br />I would have liked more details on the other boys. Stanley and Zero are given the most thorough characterization, but the other ones we know very little about. Warden is also very lightly shown and arguably she was the most interesting character. Usually I don’t care whether book is intended for younger readers or not, but in this case I can’t help the feeling I’d like the book better if I was at least 7 years younger. The book is about choosing kindness and compassion without ulterior motive, even when everything around you is hard and unfair. It is about doing your best to be happy even when there isn't much to be satisfied with. The story gave me contradicted feelings because of so many latent messages that actually made me think about what society was back then and how exactly it has changed till today. <br /><br />Stanley is convicted for a crime he didn’t commit and forced to work day after day in the hot sun, pointlessly digging holes. While loosing sense of empathy day after day, he has to learn to keep going, get along with the other boys and survive.<br /><br />I wish I'd been in Zero's head rather than Stanley's. I've got nothing against Stanley, he's an excellent narrator, but Zero was so silent all the time and I wished to know what was he thinking about when he was blankly staring at everyone around him. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15566014731318226314">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=children-middle-grade" class="actionLinkLite">children-middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1135668956">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17395041648190502730"><a title="Holes (Holes, #1) by Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38709.Holes__Holes___1_">Holes</a> is the first installment in <a title="Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6569.Louis_Sachar">Louis Sachar</a>'s middle grade/young adult series titled: <a title="Holes Boxed Set by Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15244893.Holes_Boxed_Set">Holes</a>. Again, I'm so happy to say I've found joy in reading along with my 5th grade son. This academic year has been full of fun required reading and that makes me so happy for him. It's hard to be excited about required reading but it helps so much when the content is entertaining. <br /><br />I watched the film adaptation of <a title="Holes (Holes, #1) by Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38709.Holes__Holes___1_">Holes</a> prior to reading the book, but I'm happy to say the two are almost exactly the same. Wel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17395041648190502730"><a title="Holes (Holes, #1) by Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38709.Holes__Holes___1_">Holes</a> is the first installment in <a title="Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6569.Louis_Sachar">Louis Sachar</a>'s middle grade/young adult series titled: <a title="Holes Boxed Set by Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15244893.Holes_Boxed_Set">Holes</a>. Again, I'm so happy to say I've found joy in reading along with my 5th grade son. This academic year has been full of fun required reading and that makes me so happy for him. It's hard to be excited about required reading but it helps so much when the content is entertaining. <br /><br />I watched the film adaptation of <a title="Holes (Holes, #1) by Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38709.Holes__Holes___1_">Holes</a> prior to reading the book, but I'm happy to say the two are almost exactly the same. Well done Hollywood! ...and well done <a title="Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6569.Louis_Sachar">Mr. Sachar</a> for writing a great story to begin with. Full of adventure, mystery, history; it's just fun to read (and watch). If you didn't read this during your academic years, it's not too late to check it out. Enjoy!<br /><br /><strong>My favorite quote:</strong><br /><em>“You may have done some bad things, but that doesn't mean you're a bad kid.”</em></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_66988781">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66988781" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/257424-erin" class="left imgcol" title="Erin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1186779984p2/257424.jpg" alt="Erin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/66988781?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 11, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/257424-erin" class="user" title="Erin">Erin</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer66988781">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6749527277059340110">Everybody knows who this man is, right?<br /><br />I mean, I'm looking over the reviews for this book on the front page and I can find no mention. There's not a whisper of the author's previous successes. I'm absolutely flabbergasted that the word "Wayside" is not coming up in any of my "control+F" searches. Absolutely nothing.<br /><br />"Sideways Stories from Wayside School"?! Really?! The absolute greatest story about an elementary school ever told? The one built sideways accidentally, with no 13th floor? Mrs. Gorf?</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6749527277059340110">Everybody knows who this man is, right?<br /><br />I mean, I'm looking over the reviews for this book on the front page and I can find no mention. There's not a whisper of the author's previous successes. I'm absolutely flabbergasted that the word "Wayside" is not coming up in any of my "control+F" searches. Absolutely nothing.<br /><br />"Sideways Stories from Wayside School"?! Really?! The absolute greatest story about an elementary school ever told? The one built sideways accidentally, with no 13th floor? Mrs. Gorf? Ice cream flavors that taste like people? Am I the only person on goodreads who can't do third grade long division but remembers the last names of the three Erics' in Mrs. Jewl's class?!?!?!?! (Eric Bacon, Eric Fry, and Eric Ovens)<br /><br />ANYBODY!!?!<br /><br />I am slightly confused and afraid. My universe is shifting. I thought everybody skipped their fourth boring field trip in a year to the National History Museum and read this book in the girl's bathroom. Or anywhere really. It never gets old.<br /><br />"But Erin", you might say, "This is a review of Holes. Past books shouldn't matter. As you have said before, an author is only as good as his last book. Except for Christopher Moore, who can-do-no-wrong-for- the-rest-of-eternity-forever-and-ever-amen."<br /><br />Well, normally you'd be right. But Louis Sachar's debut of Holes, I think, is much more significant for what came before it. You see, millions of little children like me had giggled and gasped through Sachar's series on a curious school with absurdly crazy characters. He was one of the first authors, like Shel Silverstein and Laura Ingalls Wilder, to have his name, and not just the title of his book, implanted in my memory. For hundreds of little children around the world, I know he was one of their first! favorite authors.<br /><br />And so, when we discovered the dog eared and dirty copy of Holes on our library shelves a couple years later, a bit older (third grade) and a bit more mature (I gave up wearing kraft cheese singles with holes bitten out of them as masks at the cafeteria table) we dove right in without a second thought.<br /><br />And oh, were we surprised.<br /><br />Holes is not the light fare I, or I think any of my friends, were expecting. I think if you try hard enough, you'll remember the first story you read in which justice was not promptly served, or the assurance of a happy ending was not guaranteed. I may have read darker tales before this one, but "Holes" was a defining moment in my childhood. Stanley went to hell on Earth and he was innocent. Nothing magical was going to help him escape, no convenient story twist was going to come along and assure you everything was a dream. Above all, no adult was gonna come get Stanley and explain that everything a big huge mistake, and he was safe and fine and protected. ADULTS knew that something horrible was happening at Camp Green Lake, and nothing was as it seemed, and no one tried to stop it.<br /><br />Stanley was so alone. And you were alone right there with him.<br /><br />Here was something much more grown up, we realized. Here is something that has the risk of death and the threat of capture and the hope of treasure and it all feels so real! Here is something that is tricky in the way it is written, not front to back like so many other simple, dumb children's authors, but has many stories all tied up together in a way that makes us think, and figure things out, and if this character and that character were with his character, could it be that---gasp!<br /><br />And I don't mean to keep speaking for the rest of the universe's little children. But I know there must have been more than just my third grade self that closed the last page of Holes and sat very very still, mouth open, staring at nothing, for a second, and realized that reading was never really going to be the same.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6749527277059340110">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_197589191">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197589191" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5945984-shelly" class="left imgcol" title="Shelly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1313081323p2/5945984.jpg" alt="Shelly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/197589191?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5945984-shelly" class="user" title="Shelly">Shelly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5945984-shelly?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer197589191">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17335787634316061223">This book really surprised me and surpassed all of my expectations for it. I loved the characters and thought the story itself was clever and nicely laid out. I never got the feeling that the author was talking down to his audience because this is a young adult novel, which is a big pet peeve of mine. Stanley and Zero were a great pair, though Zero was my favorite, and I was kept in constant suspense waiting for the next bad shoe to drop. </span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_49536340">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49536340" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1578083-jennifer" class="left imgcol" title="Jennifer"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1438076078p2/1578083.jpg" alt="Jennifer" /></a>

People kept coming in and saying "Do you have that book - Holes?" and finally I signed out a copy and read it to see what all the fuss was. It was a really good read! I immediatly understood why everyone was making a fuss over the book and why it was going to be made into a movie. (I never did see the movie.)<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_38809437">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38809437" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1734736-mary-jl" class="left imgcol" title="Mary JL"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Mary JL" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38809437?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 25, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1734736-mary-jl" class="user" title="Mary JL">Mary JL</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/285940.Holes" title="Paperback 9780747563662" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone age 11 on up</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mary JL by: </span>
      Several recommendations on GR
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1734736-mary-jl?shelf=young-adult-children" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult-children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38809437">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6151801049985760101">I know this book won the Newberry Medal--and other awards. But I must review my books for me--I rate it a very good, strong 3 stars but no higher. Defintely worth reading for anyone, however. I also freely admit--had I read this at age 12, I WOULD have rated it four stars.<br /><br />First, tops marks to the author for interlinking two stories--Stanley's incarceration at Camp Green Lake and the earlier tale of Kate Barlow. The matching and interweaving of the two plot lines is well done.<br /><br />I would have liked a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6151801049985760101">I know this book won the Newberry Medal--and other awards. But I must review my books for me--I rate it a very good, strong 3 stars but no higher. Defintely worth reading for anyone, however. I also freely admit--had I read this at age 12, I WOULD have rated it four stars.<br /><br />First, tops marks to the author for interlinking two stories--Stanley's incarceration at Camp Green Lake and the earlier tale of Kate Barlow. The matching and interweaving of the two plot lines is well done.<br /><br />I would have liked a bit more details on the other boys. Stanley and Zero are given the most detailed characterization; the other five we know little about. The Warden and the staff are also very lightly drawn. Admittedly, the author no doubt wanted to keep the book fairly short as it is intended for younger readers.<br /><br />Admittedly, a really neat scene showing cruelty without overt violence is when Stanley has annoyed a "counselor" (guard!) called Mr. Sir. They line up in the hot sun to get their canteens filled; and Mr. Sir hands Stanley's canteen back empty. Chilling--and Stanley can do nothing.<br /><br />****************spoilers below this line****************<br /><br />The 'happy everafter' ending I did not like. Stanley and Zero each get almost a million dollars. Stanley's Dad markets his invention. Clyde "Sweet Feet" Livingston comes for dinner with Stanley's family. And so on. It is just too much for me. More realistic would be if Stanley's parents had to take out a huge loan to pay for the lawyer who rescues Stanley. That is my biggest quibble with this book.<br /><br />Also, everybody makes the point that Stanley was "innocent". Even if he had been guilty, should he have been treated like he was by the Warden and the guards? Something to think about.<br /><br />Despiste my dislike of the ending, well worth reading for older children--say age 11 on up. worth reading for adults as well.<br /><br />Edited 8-25-13 to fix a few typos.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6151801049985760101">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_317732435">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317732435" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4545538-rachel-hartman" class="left imgcol" title="Rachel Hartman"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442465555p2/4545538.jpg" alt="Rachel Hartman" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/317732435?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4545538-rachel-hartman" class="user" title="Rachel Hartman">Rachel Hartman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer317732435">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2337298794187234644">I didn't think it could be done, but we finally found it: a chapter book my son and I both enjoyed equally. It wasn't too scary for him (at least not once it became clear that Stanley really was going to be able to dig that first hole -- B was super worried about him), and it wasn't too tedious for me. We both looked forward to reading it together, and even made excuses to read longer than usual each evening because we were enjoying it so much.<br /><br />I enjoyed watching my son piece together past and pr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2337298794187234644">I didn't think it could be done, but we finally found it: a chapter book my son and I both enjoyed equally. It wasn't too scary for him (at least not once it became clear that Stanley really was going to be able to dig that first hole -- B was super worried about him), and it wasn't too tedious for me. We both looked forward to reading it together, and even made excuses to read longer than usual each evening because we were enjoying it so much.<br /><br />I enjoyed watching my son piece together past and present, watching his jaw drop as he realized the way the characters' families and histories were interconnected. It's a surprisingly sophisticated narrative for a book aimed so young, and it really got him thinking about history, consequences, coincidences, and the bonds that tie us all together.<br /><br />Obviously, if you're an adult you pretty much see it coming, but it's still so much fun to watch a kid work things out and be amazed. Watching my son THINK is just about my favourite part of parenting.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2337298794187234644">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1351297208?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1166369-annet" class="user" title="Annet">Annet</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1351297208">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer612538962451139728">This book is so much fun! I used to take clippings from magazines with book reviews, found an old clipping about this book cleaning up the house recently and thought...mmm... let's read this one. Timing was impeccable. I went through an explosive challenging period of really hard work and high pressure in the office and this book made me look forward to reading if only a few pages when coming home. A quirky funny story about a boy called Stanley who is sent to 'Green Camp Lake', a boy's detentio</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText612538962451139728">This book is so much fun! I used to take clippings from magazines with book reviews, found an old clipping about this book cleaning up the house recently and thought...mmm... let's read this one. Timing was impeccable. I went through an explosive challenging period of really hard work and high pressure in the office and this book made me look forward to reading if only a few pages when coming home. A quirky funny story about a boy called Stanley who is sent to 'Green Camp Lake', a boy's detention center after supposedly having stolen a pair of sports shoes from a famous basketball player. Being innocent, he blaims his no-good-dirty-rotten-pig-stealing great-great-grandfather who ran into a curse which affected Stanley's family over years and years. Camp Green Lake is in the middle of the desert, a dried up lake, and every day a scary ward and guards, amongst who a 'Mr Sir', make the boys dig holes there. So, what's going on?....I had so much fun with this book, excellently written and the story... who can make it up? All factors combined, also the timing of this book in my life, <br />right book at the right time, couldn't be better. A sympathetic enjoyable story, really quirky and just pure FUN. Recommended!<br />ps: Curious about the movie too, never saw it (yet).</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="612538962451139728">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15937593337705461527">If you don't know this, I love young adult novels. This one especially. It might seem like just another book about young boys dealing with pride, losers versus bullies, loyalty and masculinity. But there's actually really cute and romantic story in it all. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_806211587">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/806211587" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/901342-jacob" class="left imgcol" title="Jacob"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1228116995p2/901342.jpg" alt="Jacob" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/806211587?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/901342-jacob" class="user" title="Jacob">Jacob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=movie_or_tv" class="actionLinkLite">movie_or_tv</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=youth" class="actionLinkLite">youth</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer806211587">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8791332752521788511">I know I never had this in my "currently reading" list, but I had to jump on it for the following reasons:<br /><br />1) My friend Mitchell read it recently and reminded me of it,<br /><br />2) I remembered we actually have a copy of this handy,<br /><br />3) It wouldn't be hard to complete before the end of the year, and<br /><br />4) It fits with a running theme of "books that have been made into movies", of which I've read more than a dozen this year (Tuck Everlasting, The Time Machine, I Robot, I am Number Four, Stardust, Gulliver's Trave</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8791332752521788511">I know I never had this in my "currently reading" list, but I had to jump on it for the following reasons:<br /><br />1) My friend Mitchell read it recently and reminded me of it,<br /><br />2) I remembered we actually have a copy of this handy,<br /><br />3) It wouldn't be hard to complete before the end of the year, and<br /><br />4) It fits with a running theme of "books that have been made into movies", of which I've read more than a dozen this year (Tuck Everlasting, The Time Machine, I Robot, I am Number Four, Stardust, Gulliver's Travels, The Running Man, The Shrinking Man, The Bourne Identity, Interview with the Vampire, The Great Gatsby, The Puppet Masters, and Radio Free Albemuth).<br /><br />Fortunately, the story is as good as the movie it was made into, which hasn't been the case for all the above books. Sachar's writing "style" is the same as his <a title="Sideways Stories From Wayside School (Wayside School #1) by Louis Sachar" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15779.Sideways_Stories_From_Wayside_School__Wayside_School__1_">Sideways Stories From Wayside School</a> series I enjoyed as a kid, although it could almost be considered more "no style whatsoever". The sentences and ideas tend to be short and delivered one after the other with almost no diversion, which fits a book of funny short stories better than a (short kid's) novel.<br /><br />However, there is a side benefit to this spartan writing, where Sachar writes simply, directly, and introduces one new piece of information steadily in order to expand on it in the next paragraph. It makes the storywriting very plain to anyone who is familiar with generally accepted wisdom on writing fiction. This means the method of storytelling is obvious, as are the foreshadowing and other elements. Fortunately, Sachar's story is quite good and the pieces fit together reasonably, with few loose ends. I suspect it would be well worth mapping / diagramming / analyzing to any aspiring writer.<br /><br />There are also elements of the story that I tend to enjoy, such as the "kid surviving in a school / camp" setting and the idea that who we are is directly impacted by our ancestors (one reason I like the Back to the Future trilogy so much). As it turns out, I'm named after my great-great-grandfather, although I can be relieved he wasn't no-good or pig-stealing. I also like that the characters are consistent and believable.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8791332752521788511">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_242382771">

  <a href="/user/show/5352308-eden" class="left imgcol" title="Eden"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1370573391p2/5352308.jpg" alt="Eden" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/242382771?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5352308-eden" class="user" title="Eden">Eden</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/38709.Holes" title="Paperback 9780439244190" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer242382771">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6449632774317369070">I finally went back and read this, and... stupendous. The fashion in which Louis Sachar unfolds his three stories -- four, if you count Zero's separately -- is pure wonder, 100% not from concentrate straight from the spring of genius. This is probably the only classic in elementary schools that I fully support. &lt;3<br /><br />While Stanley is the protagonist (and good thing too -- he's the one who the reader will feel closest, too), the novel really belongs to a cast of characters spanning countries and g</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6449632774317369070">I finally went back and read this, and... stupendous. The fashion in which Louis Sachar unfolds his three stories -- four, if you count Zero's separately -- is pure wonder, 100% not from concentrate straight from the spring of genius. This is probably the only classic in elementary schools that I fully support. &lt;3<br /><br />While Stanley is the protagonist (and good thing too -- he's the one who the reader will feel closest, too), the novel really belongs to a cast of characters spanning countries and generations. Elya Yelnats is probably the least complicated of the whole cast, while Katherine (or Kissin' Kate) is all the empowered female we need in this male-dominated novel.<br /><br />Where <em>Holes</em> shines is the tying together of the stories. Short snippets that, at the start, make no sense lend events later on gravity and impact and the "holy guacamole!" feeling, like the unveiling of Zero's real name (Madame Zeroni, anyone?), plus the Sploosh (Kate and her spiced peaches!), plus the yellow-spotted lizards and why they didn't kill Stanley and Zero. (You caught that flashback passage right afterward, right? Where Sam explains how they don't like onion blood? OMG. *__*)<br /><br />Yeah. I don't think I can say anything coherent beyond the fact that <em>Holes</em> is now my top-rated book. It's miraculous.<br /><br /><em>*Review originally published on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://passthechiclets.blogspot.com/2011/11/review-holes.html">Pass the Chiclets</a>.</em></span>
